  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fab56b2b-4cde-4526-bff2-dcca113b9b8a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3870136547900732539">The second book in the trilogy that launched one of the most important fantasy writers of our time.<br/><br/>It is a time of darkness, dread, and ultimate testing for the realm of Osten Ard, for the wild magic and terrifying minions of the undead Sithi ruler, Ineluki the Storm King, are spreading their seemingly undefeatable evil across the kingdom.<br/> <br/>With the very land blighted by th</span>
  <span id="freeText3870136547900732539" style="display:none">The second book in the trilogy that launched one of the most important fantasy writers of our time.<br /><br />It is a time of darkness, dread, and ultimate testing for the realm of Osten Ard, for the wild magic and terrifying minions of the undead Sithi ruler, Ineluki the Storm King, are spreading their seemingly undefeatable evil across the kingdom.<br /> <br />With the very land blighted by the power of Ineluki’s wrath, the tattered remnants of a once-proud human army flee in search of a last sanctuary and rallying point—the Stone of Farewell, a place shrouded in mystery and ancient sorrow.<br /> <br />And even as Prince Josua seeks to rally his scattered forces, Simon and the surviving members of the League of the Scroll are desperately struggling to discover the truth behind an almost-forgotten legend, which will take them from the fallen citadels of humans to the secret heartland of the Sithi—where near-immortals must at last decide whether to ally with the race of men in a final war against those of their own blood.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1149737-why-does-simon-always-faint-it-seems-like">Why does Simon always faint? It seems like every time something happens he faints, dreams, and then forget what he dreams. Does this man have memory problems or something?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1149737'><a id="like_count_community_question_1149737" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1149737?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28689.Stone_of_Farewell">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1149737-why-does-simon-always-faint-it-seems-like">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1149737-why-does-simon-always-faint-it-seems-like">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6676446-george"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1406130943i/6676446.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6676446-george">George</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think you're exaggerating, but here are a couple of answers anyway.<br/><br/>A1. It works for narrative purposes--including that he'll eventually remember and<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think you're exaggerating, but here are a couple of answers anyway.<br /><br />A1. It works for narrative purposes--including that he'll eventually remember and assemble what he's temporarily forgotten. (Not a spoiler, that statement; if it weren't true, it would be bad structure to tell us readers more than the PoV character ever knows.)<br /><br />A2. Some people, in reality and even more in fiction, do faint in such circumstances, esp. those who, like Simon, are connected to the Dream Roads ... or whatever you prefer to call the Other Side.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_492399220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492399220" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492399220?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886774806" href="/book/show/317450.Stone_of_Farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492399220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3383808010966833869">My review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91981.The_Dragonbone_Chair__Memory__Sorrow__and_Thorn___1_' title='The Dragonbone Chair (Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn, #1) by Tad Williams' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dragonbone Chair</a> did not do the novel justice. It was written in haste, a few quickly typed lines before I launched into <i>The Stone of Farewell</i>. See, <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> ended on such a note that I just <b>did.not.have.the.time</b> to think about a decent review. I simply <b>had</b> to know what happened next.<br/><br/>The first novel went to <b>great</b> pains to establish the world, so there wasn’t such a lot of exposition required for <i>The Stone of Farewell</i>. This freed the author up to do what he apparently</span>
  <span id="freeText3383808010966833869" style="display:none">My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91981.The_Dragonbone_Chair__Memory__Sorrow__and_Thorn___1_" title="The Dragonbone Chair (Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragonbone Chair</a> did not do the novel justice. It was written in haste, a few quickly typed lines before I launched into <i>The Stone of Farewell</i>. See, <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> ended on such a note that I just <b>did.not.have.the.time</b> to think about a decent review. I simply <b>had</b> to know what happened next.<br /><br />The first novel went to <b>great</b> pains to establish the world, so there wasn’t such a lot of exposition required for <i>The Stone of Farewell</i>. This freed the author up to do what he apparently does best: write awesome, and remarkably cinematic, fantasy. There is an epic sweep to <u>Memory, Sorrow and Thorn</u> that does both Tolkien and David Lean proud. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a> is on record saying that this series inspired him to write <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>.<br /> <br />Simon is a great reluctant-hero type. He is often resentful and bitter as he is swept along in the story. He rarely comprehends the significance of events and he never volunteers, but is unable to remove himself from the forefront of the stage. He often alternates between self pity and self loathing, which makes him pretty believable given the circumstances. And yet, ever so slowly, the reader starts perceiving the subtle changes, because among all the other things this novel aspires to, it is also a <i>bildungsroman</i>. As for Binabik the troll: he has to be read to be believed. There is some truth to the “dynamite in small packages” saying. The Miriamele/Aspitis sequence frustrated me to the point of orthostatic hypotension, but I have a niggling feeling that this was exactly the author’s intention. I could go on and on: the characters in here are as real as it gets in genre fiction, and there are <b>many</b> of them.<br /><br />At times touching, at times amusing, but always rousingly epic - this is the series to read if you’re into high fantasy. I don’t have the next book close at hand (it is still in the mail), which is a pity, since this one also ends on such a fever pitch that I would have loved to launch straight into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/795034.To_Green_Angel_Tower__Part_1__Memory__Sorrow__and_Thorn___3__Part_1_" title="To Green Angel Tower, Part 1 (Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn, #3; Part 1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">To Green Angel Tower, Part 1</a>, without losing momentum. Alas.<br /><br /><i>Note: Jumping into a river to attack a crocodile is probably the second stupidest thing you can do (I’m reserving judgement about the first). It didn’t affect my rating, but you might want to bear it in mind.</i> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3383808010966833869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18383883708479429142" style="display:none">A bit too long even for my taste, although, if you ask me, I don’t know what could have been cut from it. We follow our heroes’ quest throughout Osten Ard, but now we have more threads. The remaining ‘good guys’ are scattered throughout the land, each trying to reach the Stone of Farewell, the last safe bastion from the Storm King.<br /><br />There is a single wow moment, for me at least, and it was at 96%. However, there isn’t a single dull moment in the whole book. It’s just that their journeys are taking too long and I’m tired and frustrated that nothing good happens to them. Just like in LOTR, where the chain of misfortunes doesn’t seem to end for Frodo and Sam.<br /><br />Anyway, I thought I would take a break but given the revelation at the end my curiosity was piqued even more than it was so here I go on the last part of the adventure.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734150357" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11188976299269268668">As I look back on the reading experience for <i>Stone of Farewell</i>, I wonder exactly why I enjoyed it so much? I mean, not an awful lot happens. Simon returns to being a pouty, immature boy more often than not. There’s an awful lot of walking, while keeping a look-out for the bad guys. In fact, you could probably sum up the whole book in one sentence: Most of the good guys get to the Stone of Farewell.<br/><br/>I guess what made it worthwhile for me was learning quite a bit more about the Sithi (Williams’ ver</span>
  <span id="freeText11188976299269268668" style="display:none">As I look back on the reading experience for <i>Stone of Farewell</i>, I wonder exactly why I enjoyed it so much? I mean, not an awful lot happens. Simon returns to being a pouty, immature boy more often than not. There’s an awful lot of walking, while keeping a look-out for the bad guys. In fact, you could probably sum up the whole book in one sentence: Most of the good guys get to the Stone of Farewell.<br /><br />I guess what made it worthwhile for me was learning quite a bit more about the Sithi (Williams’ version of Elves). Plus getting some back-story for Ineluki, the Storm King, to find out what turned him into the vengeful creature that is threatening all of Osten Ard. There’s also a peek into Troll culture and a love interest for poor, patient old Binibik. <br /><br />The character who really gets left in the lurch in this volume is Miriamele, King Elias’ daughter. I would be reading book three regardless, but it is her fate that really is pulling me along at this point. <i>I must know what happens!</i><br /><br />This is pretty standard fantasy fare and if you enjoy high fantasy, you are likely to enjoy the <i>Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn</i> series. Those who don’t like elves, trolls, and magic swords should definitely pass this series by!<br /><br />Book 250 of my Science Fiction and Fantasy reading project.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6954156565752884105">Ok first review of 2018 and what do you know its 5 stars out of 5 <br/><br/>Anyway this book is a huge improvement on the previous book which was already fantastic, I think what stood out for me in this book was the pace and tension kept building as it wasn't like in the great hunt where it starts all over again for each book. I felt the story moved much more here than in Dragonbone chair and I was invested into what the characters were up to as they got on with there tasks set for them in Osten Ard. <br/><br/>That</span>
  <span id="freeText6954156565752884105" style="display:none">Ok first review of 2018 and what do you know its 5 stars out of 5 <br /><br />Anyway this book is a huge improvement on the previous book which was already fantastic, I think what stood out for me in this book was the pace and tension kept building as it wasn't like in the great hunt where it starts all over again for each book. I felt the story moved much more here than in Dragonbone chair and I was invested into what the characters were up to as they got on with there tasks set for them in Osten Ard. <br /><br />That is another thing I loved about this book the number of characters is just amazing and it was such a joy to revisit some (Rachel) and I was invested in all of the POV's as not only did I feel attached to the characters I was fascinated because I was learning of the huge world that is Osten Ard whether it is the mythical sites our heroes visit or the history behind certain places I loved learning about this world and being a part of it along with the characters. Simon still has a way to go but he has definitely evolved from the mooncalf back in Hayholt and I can't wait to see what he will do next because I see great things for him as he begins to mature to the Snowlock he is especially in the ultimate 1600 pages (split into 2 books of course) finale that is green angel tower<br /><br />I love this series so much the writing is exquisite, the details are so fascinating and matching it with its pace is probably the main reason why I love this book much better than the first 2 books of the wheel of time as I personally rank Osten Ard as one of my favourite fantasy world along with Roshar. I'm so glad I finally returned to this series after 9-10 months and getting into it felt like a breath of fresh air or more like cold air for this case.<br /><br />I would recommend everyone to give this series a try with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91981.The_Dragonbone_Chair__Memory__Sorrow__and_Thorn___1_" title="The Dragonbone Chair (Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragonbone Chair</a>, if you want a classical fantasy story with great worldbuilding and fine details I would start here and like I said earlier I personally enjoyed this series more than the first 2 books of the Wheel of Time series.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005178631?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841498409" href="/book/show/7404663-stone-of-farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005178631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5559246721336884076">This is book #2 in the Memory, Sorrow and Thorn series and it's a pretty classic fantasy series. I find that classic fantasy often tends to fall into some of the tropes I don't love very much (sloooooow pacing and not so developed characters were the two major complaints with this book) but when I am in the mood to read a classic fantasy series I do enjoy a good one and I think this one is that :)<br/><br/>Simon is the main character for a lot of the first book but I feel like in book two we start to bran</span>
  <span id="freeText5559246721336884076" style="display:none">This is book #2 in the Memory, Sorrow and Thorn series and it's a pretty classic fantasy series. I find that classic fantasy often tends to fall into some of the tropes I don't love very much (sloooooow pacing and not so developed characters were the two major complaints with this book) but when I am in the mood to read a classic fantasy series I do enjoy a good one and I think this one is that :)<br /><br />Simon is the main character for a lot of the first book but I feel like in book two we start to branch off into a few different plot threads and follow more people in detail. Simon is our young 'chosen one'. The boy who used to sleep in the kitchens, until he was sent off on the most important quest of all time...to find Memory, Sorrow and Thorn (3 magic swords) and hopefully fix THE WORLD :)<br /><br />We also have Binabik who is a personal favourite of the series for me. He's a troll, and he lives in a land full of trolls (well, normally he would but up until now he's been on a quest with Simon). I loved getting to see him with his people (even though they're pretty mean to him) and seeing ALL the trolls - They're kind of like cute little trolls rather than big scary ones!<br /><br />Jirki is a Sitha, one of the ancient magical races of the world who might be able to help if only they would stir themselves into action and actually worry about the destinies of mortals (can you tell I've read a few books where this happens?!)<br /><br />Prince Josua is an exiled Prince by this book and he's on the run and in hiding from the evil Norns and the others who would seek to do him harm (that's most people). He's the land's best noble chance for redemption so must be protected at all costs.<br /><br />Miriamele was the worst developed character in my opinion, she's the daughter of the crazy King (he's the reason so much of the world is an issue - or one of them) and yet ALL she seems to do is be scared, flirty, weak or whiney... I have to say from experience there's a lot more than that to a lady and she's just not a convincing character. A lot of her plot felt forced and anti-climatic to me in this book which was a shame as I think she could be great when used properly...<br /><br />Maegwin is probably one of the most far-off from the rest of the characters and the most intriguing to me. Her plot just keeps picking at me and making me wonder where it's going and how she fits into everything. She's a princess who's in hiding as the last of her line with the last of her loyal followers...<br /><br />The plot of this book certainly had some wonderful moments but equally it suffers from the slow pacing that this sort of book is known for. I don't mind a slow read when I am audio-booking (which is what I did with this one) but sometimes this felt like a lot could have been shortened/cut. <br /><br />In terms of the book as a whole I did enjoy it even though I have issues with it. It's one of the better classic fantasies I've read and I have fun being in the world, I just think it doesn't hold up alongside some of the other more modern books. It's a good adventure and I'm committed to seeing where it goes, so I am diving straight into book #3 and will report back. 3*s for this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5559246721336884076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12399032380636334340">  The apocalypse that has befallen the world of Osten Ard is fully unveiled. It might be a slow unravelling but it is a very satisfying one. The worldbuilding is tremendous. Our view of the world expands and its full of magnificent places, people and their stories. Especially the various subraces of the elvenkind are awesome. Apart from the Middle Earth this is the only place that I can say that I love the Elves. They share the grandeur and the drama of their Tolkien counterparts but they are at</span>
  <span id="freeText12399032380636334340" style="display:none">  The apocalypse that has befallen the world of Osten Ard is fully unveiled. It might be a slow unravelling but it is a very satisfying one. The worldbuilding is tremendous. Our view of the world expands and its full of magnificent places, people and their stories. Especially the various subraces of the elvenkind are awesome. Apart from the Middle Earth this is the only place that I can say that I love the Elves. They share the grandeur and the drama of their Tolkien counterparts but they are at the same time very original and unique. <br />  I also liked a lot the horror and darker elements that appeared in bigger numbers. The enemy is spreading like a plague and the world is turning fast to a menacing and dangerous place. <br />   I dont know if that kind of storytelling would appeal to everyone. Especially to people who prefer faster and action oriented stories but if you like a more romantic and adventurous approach u ll probably appreciate these books a lot.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26047418-stone-of-farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1126371-kitvaria-sarene?shelf=fantasy-no-subgenre">fantasy-no-subgenre</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1772008847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17207918445661625850">It has been about 7 years since I read the first book - and it took me quite a while to get back into the story. Once I remembered the multitude of characters, I was quickly sucked in again.<br/>On the one hand I really enjoyed the story - on the other hand it was veeeery long in places. A lot of description, that didn't feel entirely necessary in some scenes - while at other places it felt perfectly balanced, even though it had some minute details.<br/><br/>What bugged me (as everyone knowing me will expect) </span>
  <span id="freeText17207918445661625850" style="display:none">It has been about 7 years since I read the first book - and it took me quite a while to get back into the story. Once I remembered the multitude of characters, I was quickly sucked in again.<br />On the one hand I really enjoyed the story - on the other hand it was veeeery long in places. A lot of description, that didn't feel entirely necessary in some scenes - while at other places it felt perfectly balanced, even though it had some minute details.<br /><br />What bugged me (as everyone knowing me will expect) was that there was quite some being in love in this one. Thankfully not a full love story, but a princess in love with someone, a prince in love with someone, and a mooncalf boy in love with someone. Or other. It wasn't overly much - but mentioned quite often, and I simply hate romance in my fantasy- especially if it doesn't really feel like a natural part of the story.<br /><br />I very much enjoyed the different characters - I liked how the different races and cultures actually felt different to each other, and not just like "Smaller human", "human with magic" and such! (Special Kudos to the audible narrator who manages to give them different accents, and ways of speaking who fit perfectly!) I also liked the richness of the world and the way you don't feel like if you look behind a tree there would be a blank wall, but as if you were in the world, and the world was real. (And yes, I think that would still have been possible with some less flowery descriptions here and there.)<br /><br />I thought some of the characters actions overly naive, and it had quite an episodic feel to it in places - also the fight scenes were a bit predictable and I had a deja vu of LOTR - and they are walking (or sometimes riding in this one) and walking, and still walking, and more walking and how surprising - even more walking! ;)<br /><br />All in all definitely still a good series, and I will try my best not to wait 7 years again before I will pick up book three!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17207918445661625850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16546631159329671192">++SPOILERS++<br/><br/>Whereas the first book was a nice comfort read, this one gave me anxiety through much of it.<br/><br/>Lots of stuff going on, a bit more conflict but few resolutions, which I expect will come in the last book.<br/><br/>There is alot of back and fourth with different characters POV's as they all strive to their own purposes.<br/><br/>I have grown to dislike Mirabele, who in the first book seemed strong but has now turned to a stupid shallow child. I hate that she gave herself to the earl..little whore.. I also hat</span>
  <span id="freeText16546631159329671192" style="display:none">++SPOILERS++<br /><br />Whereas the first book was a nice comfort read, this one gave me anxiety through much of it.<br /><br />Lots of stuff going on, a bit more conflict but few resolutions, which I expect will come in the last book.<br /><br />There is alot of back and fourth with different characters POV's as they all strive to their own purposes.<br /><br />I have grown to dislike Mirabele, who in the first book seemed strong but has now turned to a stupid shallow child. I hate that she gave herself to the earl..little whore.. I also hated the slut sithi who kept hanging all over Simon..but at least he turned her away.<br /><br />Men just have no clue how to write romance. This author also seems to have a low opinion of women for all the women characters are dreadful. They all seem pitiful, shallow and weak.<br /><br />I am hoping this changes in the next book.<br /><br />I do still love Simon, and it is his character that keeps me going.<br /><br />The pace in this book is a little faster, but the author still over does it with flowery descriptions and I found myself skimming at times, I just wanted to scream..get on with it!<br /><br />It also seemed there is alot of writing about crap that doesn't reveal much. I can't really explain it but I read paragraphs and paragraphs and find the characters don't learn anything new or go anywhere.<br /><br />I know this sound negative considering I gave 4 stars, in truth it was a good book, but perhaps it is just that the writing style is a little outdated. The story itsself is good so I will continue.<br /><br />Safety: Blood, violence. No cursing. Sex implied for Mirabele.<br /><br />Romance peeps: Mirabele who is supposed to end up with Simon, sleeps with another. Simon is tempted by another but resists. Josua still doesn't love his woman but she loves him. They marry because she is pregnant. Binabik marries his love but has to leave her behind.<br /></span>

<div id="review_282911808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282911808" />
    <a title="Aldi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1200744-aldi"><img alt="Aldi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508567545p2/1200744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282911808?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aldi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aldi" href="/user/show/1200744-aldi">Aldi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=all-the-feelings">all-the-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=rereads-to-break-you-all-over-again">rereads-to-break-you-all-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=all-time-favs">all-time-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer282911808&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282911808" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6233142517776435760">A.k.a. The One Where Everything Goes Pearshaped.<br/><br/>Which is pretty awesome, let's be honest. I think my favourite thing here is how the story opens up into this phenomenally epic thing - not that the first book wasn't epic, but we still mostly stayed close to Simon and his journey. This book is where we truly get to know some of the other characters on a deeper level, while also exploring more parts of the world itself. I mean, hello, Isgrimnur playing at being a monk? Guthwulf discovering he may n</span>
  <span id="freeText6233142517776435760" style="display:none">A.k.a. The One Where Everything Goes Pearshaped.<br /><br />Which is pretty awesome, let's be honest. I think my favourite thing here is how the story opens up into this phenomenally epic thing - not that the first book wasn't epic, but we still mostly stayed close to Simon and his journey. This book is where we truly get to know some of the other characters on a deeper level, while also exploring more parts of the world itself. I mean, hello, Isgrimnur playing at being a monk? Guthwulf discovering he may not want to stick this one out with his old war-buddy who's essentially become a dangerous madman? Jao é-Tinukai'i? Gimme a holiday there right now (although I'm with Simon, it would be nice to be able to leave eventually :p)<br /><br />I have so many favourite parts in this it's hard to even choose. One of the journeys I love best has to be Josua &amp; Co. on their trek east, how they run into the Thrithings people and how he and Vorzheva slowly begin to develop a deeper understanding for each other (yeah, I can never help rooting for those crazy kids and their completely opposing personalities). And I love a good rebellion, so seeing Josua (quiet, bookish, stand-offish Josua) inspire loyalty from new followers and becoming a beacon of hope was just lovely.<br /><br />I seem to recall that I wasn't that taken with Miriamele's parts when I first read this a long time ago, but that's completely changed since - she's so lonely and desperate to make a difference in the world, and my heart ached for her when she was continually thwarted. (Can we have a massive kick in the balls for Aspitis every time he appears, please? Horrid smarmy git!) And Cadrach, too - he may well be one of the fundamentally saddest characters I've ever encountered, and I wish something could go right for him, just once. <br /><br />Also, while on the subject of Miri, let's talk about the women in general for a moment, because this is one of the best female casts in fantasy ever. I still have that soft spot (and ok, major crush) on Vorzheva and her utter lack of patience for nonsense. She rocks, and while I delighted in her pig of a father getting humiliated by Josua, I still wish she had had a bit more of a hand in it herself, but oh well. Then there's Geloë - I think we can all agree that the rebellion would never have stood a chance without her saving their sorry arses at every opportunity, Y/Y? And I love how she basically thinks humans are all morons, but she still keeps helping them out, lol. There's also Rachel, of course, so diminished now that everything in "her" castle has gone horribly wrong, but also still so formidable. I mean, who else would go for the most sensible/straightforward solution and just stick a dagger in that creep Pryrates? That woman deserves a medal.<br /><br />And Aditu, of course. Mrow. I'm very glad that although the Sithi have their similarities to other elf races in fantasy (it's hard to avoid that), Tad gave them some customs and characteristics that are unique to this world and their culture - the wealth of colour they surround themselves with, the fact that they are obviously not asexual, the hints that at least some of them are not at all content to pass quietly from the world. But back to Aditu, I love how irreverent and mocking she is about mortal silliness, but how the relationship she and Simon develop is still something real and mutually intrigued. <br /><br />I can't quite bear to think about Eolair and Maegwin yet, because their constantly crossed wires and misunderstandings are just so devastating. TALK TO EACH OTHER, YOU STUBBORN FOOLS! Arrrgh. <br /><br />Anyway. The descriptions still take my breath away and the pacing never misses a beat. It's just one of those enviably flawless books, and I don't mean it has no mistakes ever or that the writing is always perfect - I mean that the world is so rich and the story and characters have such depth that you find yourself pulled right in and reluctant to be lured back out by some boring RL thing. It's been an immensely enjoyable reread, and I can't wait to follow these good old friends to the end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6233142517776435760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752219416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1854770988862754939">When I first read this book twenty years ago I was frustrated with the side characters/stories because I had no patience and thought this story should be about Seoman alone. Now I can laugh at how foolish and shallow I was and marvel at how beautiful the story truly is. Tiamak's inner struggles alone would be worth a story about. This is an excellently crafted tale that adds depth and life to this trilogy. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4540891112067005477">On my third (possibly fourth) reading of this book, I realized something: it was just as good as the first time I read it.<br/><br/>The splendid cast of characters, all real individuals, are just as engrossing. The layers of plot (and plotting) are just as tight and as fascinating.<br/><br/>Thus I maintain my stance that this is one of the best fantasy series of all time.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_51024539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51024539" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_124258245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124258245" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124258245?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886774806" href="/book/show/317450.Stone_of_Farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=wizardy-magic">wizardy-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124258245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7823534629891322788"><i>Stone of Farewell</i>, the sequel to <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> and the second book in the Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn epic fantasy series continues the journey of our cast of main characters - quite literally.<br/><br/>Simon and his friends might have found the sword Thorn, but a single sword is not enough to bring down King Elias. Meanwhile, Prince Josua flees from the Norn that have destroyed his army and his city. Miriamele and the mysterious Father Cadrach try to reach her uncle to appeal to him and get his to s</span>
  <span id="freeText7823534629891322788" style="display:none"><i>Stone of Farewell</i>, the sequel to <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> and the second book in the Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn epic fantasy series continues the journey of our cast of main characters - quite literally.<br /><br />Simon and his friends might have found the sword Thorn, but a single sword is not enough to bring down King Elias. Meanwhile, Prince Josua flees from the Norn that have destroyed his army and his city. Miriamele and the mysterious Father Cadrach try to reach her uncle to appeal to him and get his to support Josua in his cause.<br /><br />In <i>Stone of Farewell</i> almost all of the main characters are on some kind of trip or mission. I wouldn't want to say that this novel suffers from being a second book, but it <i>is</i> clear when reading that this is a middle book. It deals with the repercussions of the events that end <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i>, and follows the main characters as they start to get ready for their final stand against Elias in the final novel of the trilogy. For the longest time I felt that everything would go wrong. The situation for almost all parties is precarious. But in the end Mr Williams pulled it off admirably, never resorting to the unbelievable to bring everyone together.<br /><br />What struck me when reading this is how many similarities there are between the Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn books and those of the Song of Ice and Fire series. Tad William's trilogy predates <i>Game of Thrones</i> by several years, and it's clear that George R.R. Martin has read these books and found them inspiring. Where Martin keeps reminding us that "winter is coming", winter in <i>Stone of Farewell</i> already has come. Under influence of the Storm King in the north, huenen have left their lairs and are coming south with winter in their wake. Sound familiar? Additionally, the way Williams uses many points of view to tell his story is further developed by Martin in his infamous endless points of view. I got to admit, all of the characters are way easier to keep track of in Williams' books.<br /><br />For me <i>Stone of Farewell</i> hit all the spots. It has everything I look for in epic fantasy. A reluctant hero who grows up throughout the story, competent female characters, an unspeakable evil that threatens the world order, and a whole cast of people with unclear allegiances. I have no doubt the evil will be defeated by the end of the trilogy, but the journey comes with a price.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7823534629891322788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6604486436815404989">I feel we have a much larger cast in this book compared to the first in the trilogy, and it's so much the better for it, as we <i>usually</i> get to skip past the boring stuff and visit other plot threads doing interesting things. However, it suffers a bit from middle-book-syndrome, especially once you realize by the end that we ended up with 3 different groups of people just aiming to get to a single point. I'm very curious to see how this story will progress.<br/><br/>The final book will likely satisfy, but it</span>
  <span id="freeText6604486436815404989" style="display:none">I feel we have a much larger cast in this book compared to the first in the trilogy, and it's so much the better for it, as we <i>usually</i> get to skip past the boring stuff and visit other plot threads doing interesting things. However, it suffers a bit from middle-book-syndrome, especially once you realize by the end that we ended up with 3 different groups of people just aiming to get to a single point. I'm very curious to see how this story will progress.<br /><br />The final book will likely satisfy, but it's also a literal monster (at around 550,000 words, which is at least 100,000 more than the longest Sanderson book, and even longer than any Jordan or Martin book), so I'm kind of dreading it.</span>

<div id="review_2672854544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672854544" />
    <a title="Matthew Quann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann"><img alt="Matthew Quann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528393487p2/22699228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2672854544?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Quann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Quann" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann">Matthew Quann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0756402976" href="/book/show/33898831-stone-of-farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=big-books-500-pages-plus">big-books-500-pages-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2672854544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7916976347483801777">While I loved the world-building and moderate pace of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867814715?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i>
</a>, I found myself missing the compulsive readability of a lot of modern fantasy. All the same, there were nuggets of classic fantasy I read as a fledgling that stoked the fires of nostalgia, while the signs of fantasy pivoting from its roots gave me a bit of historical satisfaction. You can imagine my pleasure when I discovered that <i>Stone of Farewell</i> picks up the pace and deepens the richness of Osten Ard.<br/><br/>I found myself</span>
  <span id="freeText7916976347483801777" style="display:none">While I loved the world-building and moderate pace of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867814715?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i>
</a>, I found myself missing the compulsive readability of a lot of modern fantasy. All the same, there were nuggets of classic fantasy I read as a fledgling that stoked the fires of nostalgia, while the signs of fantasy pivoting from its roots gave me a bit of historical satisfaction. You can imagine my pleasure when I discovered that <i>Stone of Farewell</i> picks up the pace and deepens the richness of Osten Ard.<br /><br />I found myself floundering a bit with the huge cast in the first book, but each of the POV characters in this book became more fleshed out and their roles more comprehensible. The various houses, peoples, and lands of the world were starting to come into focus when I started this novel, but I'm comfortable with all the major bits now. What's more, there were many scenes peppered throughout this sequel that rivalled the excitement of the original's concluding action piece. I love the way Williams makes the plight of our heroes seem so hopeless, yet the leads persist to often stirring results.<br /><br />Looking forward, the third book in the trilogy is perhaps most daunting of all. It clocks in at a whopping 1000 pages, and you just have to wonder how much of that will be slightly dull travelogue. If the trend continues, I expect that there'll be a fair bit of travel, but much less than either of the first two books Despite those misgivings, I've really enjoyed how Williams leaves room for the world to breathe, giving it a feeling of a place well lived-in. I'm also looking forward to how Williams is able to wrap up the trilogy and answer questions I'm surprised he's yet to touch on. <br /><br />First, a little palate-cleansing! <br /><br />*Reviewer's note: I'll be waiting to finish the entire trilogy before providing a comprehensive review. Once I'm done with <i>To Green Angel Tower</i>, I'll publish a trilogy-review to better encapsulate the scope and arc of this story! So check back later for a full review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7916976347483801777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3484064278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3484064278" />
    <a title="Doug" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33038913-doug"><img alt="Doug" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515035780p2/33038913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3484064278?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug" href="/user/show/33038913-doug">Doug</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3484064278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17547136103589227701">This book basically captures the worst parts of middle-book syndrome: it's more of unrewarding slog than it had any right to be, because the underlying plot and characters are really quite good. But they are packaged here in a way that is really... unfortunate for the reader.<br/><br/>The whole plot revolves around getting to the Stone of Farewell, and this plot is just stretched way too thin. It doesn't help that the author is holding every single card close to his vest, and it gets really frustrating to</span>
  <span id="freeText17547136103589227701" style="display:none">This book basically captures the worst parts of middle-book syndrome: it's more of unrewarding slog than it had any right to be, because the underlying plot and characters are really quite good. But they are packaged here in a way that is really... unfortunate for the reader.<br /><br />The whole plot revolves around getting to the Stone of Farewell, and this plot is just stretched way too thin. It doesn't help that the author is holding every single card close to his vest, and it gets really frustrating to not get any answers. This problem is exacerbated by the fact that I desperately wanted some reason to get excited about what's coming, in order to feel like this slog was justified. Ultimately, the answer to whether it was justified will sadly come only in the last book. If this book had been a third, or even a quarter, of the length, or simply not existed at all and its contents consolidated into the preceding or following book, I think this series would have been an excellent duology. But the pacing here sucks, which is a shame because everything else is so cool.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17547136103589227701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2359029522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2359029522" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2359029522?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8498843-stone-of-farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2359029522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8687476183435290896">There are many things about this series which are just rather typical. You can predict a lot of the narrative beats and tropes, because it’s drawing from the same well of story as a lot of other epic fantasy. However, if you made it through the first book (a feat in itself just because of how long it is), you’re probably aware of that and on board for the characters. And I’m pleased to note that they don’t disappoint: Simon gets less annoying, Rachel the Dragon continues to play her part, Binabi</span>
  <span id="freeText8687476183435290896" style="display:none">There are many things about this series which are just rather typical. You can predict a lot of the narrative beats and tropes, because it’s drawing from the same well of story as a lot of other epic fantasy. However, if you made it through the first book (a feat in itself just because of how long it is), you’re probably aware of that and on board for the characters. And I’m pleased to note that they don’t disappoint: Simon gets less annoying, Rachel the Dragon continues to play her part, Binabik’s background is explored somewhat, there’s more of Jiriki… and most importantly to me, remembering that he was my favourite character before, there’s more of Josua. Although, on this read-through, I might actually be preferring Deornoth…<br /><br />In any case, the story barrels along at a reasonable pace, and though there are one or two sticking points, it never slows up as much as the first half to two-thirds of the first book. I remembered somewhat why I’d found a particular character so annoying, which was a little disappointing after rather enjoying their part (such as it was) in the first book.<br /><br />Pryrates remains an excellent villain of the cackling evil laugh sort, doing evil things with little remorse. Elias is a little more grey-shaded, but really not much: this series up to this point has a pretty black-and-white view of morality, with the Sithi perhaps being the most subtle element.<br /><br />I’m enjoying it very much for what it is: very much drawn from fantasy tropes, but with a solid cast of characters who don’t fall too easily into stereotypes.<br /><br /><a href="https://breathesbooks.com/2018/02/27/review-the-stone-of-farewell/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reviewed for the Bibliophibian.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8687476183435290896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_354450187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354450187" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10152557-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409575790p2/10152557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354450187?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/10152557-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886774806" href="/book/show/317450.Stone_of_Farewell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10152557-scott?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10152557-scott?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354450187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11680695399191983247">This one is a tough one for me.<br/>It's a re-read and I haven't read this book since it was first released 30 so years ago.<br/>My memory has always told me that it's my favorite fantasy series of all time and I loved the last book...this one was not as good.<br/>The writing is beautiful, almost poetic.<br/>The characters are amazing, probably a hundred or so, all fully formed. Interesting, conflicted, complex.<br/>The plot is just what I like - epic, huge, sprawling, majestic.<br/>But<br/>This book was slow and let's be serious</span>
  <span id="freeText11680695399191983247" style="display:none">This one is a tough one for me.<br />It's a re-read and I haven't read this book since it was first released 30 so years ago.<br />My memory has always told me that it's my favorite fantasy series of all time and I loved the last book...this one was not as good.<br />The writing is beautiful, almost poetic.<br />The characters are amazing, probably a hundred or so, all fully formed. Interesting, conflicted, complex.<br />The plot is just what I like - epic, huge, sprawling, majestic.<br />But<br />This book was slow and let's be serious here...not much happened.<br />No matter how great the writing, if you are going to give me 800 pages then make something happen. Don't get me wrong, this is no Robert Jordan book. Things are constantly happening and the plot is always moving forward but there just was no grand point, plot, event that actually happened.<br /><br />Is it the standard "2nd book syndrome" which holds the series together between book 1 and 3? <br />I don't know at the moment because it's been 30 years since I read book 3 so the I have long forgotten all the details.<br /><br />I'm being hard on the book but only because in my memory this is a 6 star book.<br />It is still very very very very good and I would recommend it to anyone, and recommend it twice to some people.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to the conclusion of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11680695399191983247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1899887658?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/203607-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/203607-jenn?shelf=highlyrecommend">highlyrecommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/203607-jenn?shelf=all-timefaves">all-timefaves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/203607-jenn?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1899887658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11196331438981545520">This amazing fantasy series continues in the second volume with more excellent plotting, characterizations, and world-building. It reminds me of the Two Towers, which is also a "middle" novel, where events continue to progress from the first novel (and there's a lot of traveling and characters moving around). I'm impressed with Williams' ability to create so many characters who are given interesting roles and backgrounds, and to weave their stories so effortlessly, but sometimes feel resentful w</span>
  <span id="freeText11196331438981545520" style="display:none">This amazing fantasy series continues in the second volume with more excellent plotting, characterizations, and world-building. It reminds me of the Two Towers, which is also a "middle" novel, where events continue to progress from the first novel (and there's a lot of traveling and characters moving around). I'm impressed with Williams' ability to create so many characters who are given interesting roles and backgrounds, and to weave their stories so effortlessly, but sometimes feel resentful when the plot jumps away from a character right at a crucial moment and sends us to two or three other places, before picking up the narrative thread. (But, I am an impatient person who gets so into the story and the intensity, that I can't be patient!) My favorite character continues to be Simon, who reminds me of Harry Potter in my favorite of that series, The Order of the Phoenix, because he acts exactly like an angry, emotion-ridden teen who is on the threshold of adulthood, and it's very realistic. He has so many great and also human qualities and I love reading his story in particular.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11196331438981545520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48451466-max?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460876572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3574513985093544181">This is one of my favourite series, ever. Tad Williams is my favourite author of fantasy. I met him once, and he is also hilariously funny and a good guy.<br/><br/>So, I can not give an unbiased review, hee hee. :-) Only praise for this series and everything else Tad writes.<br/><br/>I was looking for fantasy books like Lord of the Rings when someone recommended me this. And while you shouldn't compare anything to Tolkien in terms of writing (my humble opinion), these books are a whole different category. So I can </span>
  <span id="freeText3574513985093544181" style="display:none">This is one of my favourite series, ever. Tad Williams is my favourite author of fantasy. I met him once, and he is also hilariously funny and a good guy.<br /><br />So, I can not give an unbiased review, hee hee. :-) Only praise for this series and everything else Tad writes.<br /><br />I was looking for fantasy books like Lord of the Rings when someone recommended me this. And while you shouldn't compare anything to Tolkien in terms of writing (my humble opinion), these books are a whole different category. So I can not say this is better than Lord of the Rings, or LotR is better than this, but it's alongside each other, just as great, but just different. I found these books to be easier to read, while LotR is more intense. <br /><br />I will stop comparing now, haha. Anyway, don't be daunted by the gazillion pages, if you're into fantasy you will breeze through them and after the three books you'll actually want more. So glad the author is still writing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3574513985093544181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k5KVHnFCrrYMotYV4dESTrMAgp4GO7MRKRcdxvmR/9kmKm0pqD/bzOYYkscwKpjUfbyZ8MjuJVwy7T4IjnNvXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GOrPAT7rJw820NFicLgXK2cVxJd5wlhtZTY+nPzhZsCtUjc255ZSddxqlbChQ52xqanf+bcXziB+zB1SiwP2RQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8440435620430963051">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an</span>
  <span id="freeText8440435620430963051" style="display:none">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an MMO on steam.com. Tad is currently immersed in the creation of ‘The Last King of Osten Ard’, planned as a trilogy with two intermediary novels. He, his family and his animals live in the Santa Cruz mountains in a suitably strange and beautiful house. @tadwilliams @mrstad</span>
